"Welcome to the AI engineer perspective experience! Before you go through the door to continue onto the exhibits, we would like to explain to you the museum's purpose and overarching goal. The question that this experience was made to answer is: How can the public’s knowledge and experience with AI make it harder for companies to use it unethically? As artificial intelligence continues to advance and be incorporated into society, it is important for the public to educate and familiarize themselves with AI. If artificial intelligence is introduced/incorporated into an uneducated public, the companies in control of the AI could be allowed to use the AI in unethical ways. However, if the public is educated about the possible applications of AI, then they will be aware of the unethical ways that it could be used and take preventive actions. It is suggested that you keep this concept and question in mind while exploring the exhibits. Through the perspective of the AI engineer, you will examine the effect that knowledge and experience with AI have on one's understanding and appreciation of AI applications. The engineer will examine different areas/types of AI applications and how they can be applied ethically and unethically within society. After the completion of the AI engineer experience, it is highly recommended to return to the start and explore the exhibits again through the perspective of ordinary members of society. This will allow you to clearly see the importance of educating the public on the dangerous and unethical applications of AI. But first... [[Cognitive Science Applications|cognittive science applications 01]] [[Natural Interface Applications|natural interface applications 01]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= The green arrow appears again guiding you through the door towards the immediate right-hand side of the hallway. Text appears above an alcove on the wall saying ''Cognitive Science Applications.'' Bellow in the alcove: Cognitive science is often described as the study of the cognitive functioning of the human mind and the underlying mental processes through the integration of numerous disciplines such as neuroscience, computer science, psychology, artificial intelligence (AI), philosophy, linguistics, and anthropology. Research focuses on understanding the essence/nature of the human mind and how it uses mental perceptions to manipulate and process knowledge. Researchers strive to accomplish this level of understanding by investigating the inner workings of nervous systems that facilitate essential mental faculties such as perception, memory, emotional experience, learning, reasoning, problem-solving, decision-making, and language. Cognitive science and artificial intelligence research/development are very closely connected and have been since both of their emergences in the 1950s. Both programs have remained connected and have shared most advancements and applications since. Cognitive science seeks to comprehend intelligence's underlying principles to obtain a more complete understanding of the mind and learning. Similarly, AI is the simulation/mimic of human intelligence by computerized programs. NLP enables AI programs the ability to communicate with humans through language, read text, interpret speech, measure tone and recognize important points. A current research focus for many working on NLP programs is incorporating language processing into programming. With this introduction, the overly complex and incoherent programming languages used today like JavaScript, Python, HTML, CSS, etc., can be replaced with natural (human) language. <W> <img src="https://img.freepik.com/free-vector/natural-language-processing-illustration_23-2149226911.jpg?w=2000&t=st=1670902939~exp=1670903539~hmac=88d89eef8a04476a29448a314d6276c03b733ef3cbbc050333fab6456811dfdb" width="600px" height="300px"/> ^^Image by <a href="https://www.freepik.com/free-vector/natural-language-processing-illustration_21743712.htm#query=natural%20language%20processing&position=0&from_view=search&track=sph">Freepik</a>^^ <R>Natural language processing programs might seem a little too similar to speech recognition programs and you would be entirely wrong. NLP programs sometimes make use of speech recognition programs, but only when they are being spoken to. NLPs are not only for speech, these programs process any type of written, typed, or spoken language from around the world. The essential difference between an NLP and a speech recognition program is the processing. The latter simply recognizes speech while NLPs understand/analyze natural language and are able to generate a response. There are numerous ways that natural language processing can benefit society, however, like most things in this world, the applications of NLPs that could benefit society can be used in the same/similar ways to harm society. Below are applications of NLP AI programs that were intended to benefit society but then were taken advantage of to cause harm to society: <R> (align:"<==")[=[[Chat Bots]] [[Writing/summary programs]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[=[[Speech Recognition]] [[Mental Interface]] [[Virtual Reality]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]] [[Cognitive Science Application]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= (b4r:"none","none","double")+(b4r-size:1.5,1.5,2)+(b4r-colour:yellow,yellow,white)[''Speech Recognition''] Speech recognition refers to a computer or program that is able to interpret words spoken by a human and convert the information into a format legible to computers. Speech recognition AI applications have grown in popularity in recent years, as businesses increasingly use digital assistants and automated support to optimize their services. Speech recognition has gained popularity in applications such as voice assistants, smart home devices, search engines, and so on. Speech recognition has become an integral part of our lives, from smart home devices and appliances that receive orders and can be turned on and off remotely, to digital assistants that can create reminders, plan meetings, recognize a song playing in a pub, and search engines that react with appropriate search results to search queries. <img src="https://www.infoholicresearch.com/images/media/speech-recognition-technology1.jpg"/> Image by Freepix:https://www.freepik.com/ <R>Through the use of artificial intelligence and machine learning, speech recognition is rapidly overcoming the obstacles of poor recording equipment, variances in people's voices, accents, dialects, semantics, contexts, etc. This also includes difficulties in comprehending human disposition and the many human language aspects such as colloquialisms, acronyms, and so on. When compared to previous methods of speech recognition, the technology can now achieve 95% accuracy, which is on par with typical human conversation. These applications have dramatically improved aspects of our lives like organization, and time management, and making information about almost everything in everyday life more convenient to access. This information was already easily accessible and convenient to anybody with a smartphone in their pocket, now with improved speech recognition programs, we don't have to bother with typing anymore. We can just say “Hey Siri, what is the temperature outside?” instead of having to exhaust ourselves labouring to open the weather app to check. However, this convenience comes at a cost. Many of these speech recognition/speech-activated programs constantly have their microphone turned on to be able to identify when they are needed. Some companies design these programs to monitor conversations overheard by the product to listen for any mention of useful data. This data is usually sold to advertising firms who promote specific products to you based on what was overheard by the program. <R> [[Natural Language Processing]] [[Mental Interface]] [[Virtual Reality]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]] [[Cognitive Science Application]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= (b4r:"none","none","double")+(b4r-size:1.5,1.5,2)+(b4r-colour:yellow,yellow,white)[''Virtual Reality''] Virtual Reality(VR) is the creation of a realistic world in a digital environment. Realistic may not be the best word to use because these programs are not always realistic in the sense that they are life-like, as the most used application of VR is in the form of video games that may be animated. To qualify something as being a/in virtual reality and the reason why realistic is still used in the definition, the user must be placed in a virtual 3D environment (wearing a VR headset) in which they can move around the space and interact with or manipulate objects around them as if they were there in real life. Virtual reality and artificial intelligence have been developing independently from each other but with recent advancements in both fields, they are finally being put together to make extraordinary programs. Possibly the most impressive combination of these 2 technologies is the hyper-realistic racecar simulators used for esports and the training of professional racers. There are many impressive VR simulators out there but few are as immersive as those utilized by professional racecar drivers for training. <iframe width="560" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/2ct1q5dF-uY" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen></iframe> ^^DISCLAIMER - Video contains minor swearing in french with english subtitles.^^ <iframe width="560" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/1uzHazKkZ4o" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen></iframe> <R>The main benefit received from using AI to help develop VR simulation programs is a dramatic increase in the accuracy and authenticity of the simulation. Through the input of hours of racing footage and data collected by sensors attached to cars going around different tracks (usually hundreds of times), AI programs are able to use machine learning to develop the most accurate game possible. The sensors are attached all over the interior and exterior of the car and are meant to detect specific statistics concerning G-force, tire friction, aerodynamics, power-to-weight ratios, horsepower, etc., of different types of cars. The more training data an AI program has to analyze, the more accurate the game, so numerous race conditions are changed as many times as possible while recording data. If you are not familiar with the concept of the extraordinary film “Ready Player One”, the public is obsessed with this massive immersive VR world called the Oasis where anyone can be anyone/anything and do whatever they want. The presence of a separate virtual world/universe to the extent of the Oasis in our society comes with some obvious problems. However, I am most uneasy about the presence of AI in this world and how the programs would be treated by the community. Given that they have human-level or near-human-level intelligence and could be considered conscious, they should be granted some variation of human rights. If this becomes the case, the next problem we encounter is if the community would respect these human rights since the AI will only be a program without a physical body.<R> [[Natural Language Processing]] [[Speech Recognition]] [[Mental Interface]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]] [[Cognitive Science Application]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= (b4r:"none","none","double")+(b4r-size:1.5,1.5,2)+(b4r-colour:yellow,yellow,white)[''Expert Systems''] Expert Systems are machines that have been trained to have complete expertise in specific subjects of interest. These machines are designed and developed to solve specific problems. Through a logical progression of yes-or-no questions, these systems use statistical analysis and data mining to deduce answers to these challenges. ''Expert systems are comprised of 3 main parts:'' ''User Interface:''Through the user interface expert systems can interact with the user to receive prompts/inquiries which it then passes on to the inference engine. ''An interface that allows the non-expert user to engage with the expert system to receive an answer.'' ''Inference/Rules Engine:''Considered by many to be the brain of the expert system since it is responsible for the majority of the processing power in the system. To service a user's inquiry, the system applies inference rules(search filters) to the knowledge base to formulate a response/answer. There are 2 types of inference engines, deterministic and probabilistic. Deterministic engines formulate conclusions derived from facts and rules and thus is considered the more reliable of the 2. Probabilistic engines usually formulate conclusions based on probability which brings uncertainty to their responses. ''Knowledge Base:''Similar to a database, the knowledge base is responsible for the storage of all the information, rules, data, and connections that are necessary for the expert system to have total expertise on their assigned subject. In the same way that the inference engines are separated into 2 categories, the information in the knowledge bases are organized into 2 main categories, factual knowledge and heuristic knowledge. Factual knowledge is exactly as it sounds, while heuristic knowledge is based on practice, the ability to guess, evaluate, and experience. <img src="https://static.javatpoint.com/tutorial/ai/images/expert-systems-in-ai.png"/> Image Found on:https://www.javatpoint.com/expert-systems-in-artificial-intelligence <R> Recent technological advancements and innovations have made it possible for scientists to stimulate the human brain using a computerized system with much more precision and accuracy. In simpler terms, recent advancements in cognitive science AI have ensured the utilization of the full potential of computers to supplement/replicate the thinking ability of human beings. The advancement of expert systems to the point that they surpass human intelligence can fabricate numerous opportunities for these systems to be exploited and applied in unethical ways. The more expert system AI is used the more knowledgeable it can become. With continued development, these can pose a significant threat to society in the form of increased misinformation (if the knowledge base isn't updated regularly). Another threat posed by these systems would depend on if they are allowed to compete against humans in games like poker and betting as well as competitions in general. If they are allowed, they would have an unfair advantage over their flesh-bodied predecessor.<R> [[Learning Systems]] [[Neural Networks]] [[Intelligent Agents]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]] [[Natural Interface Applications]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= (b4r:"none","none","double")+(b4r-size:1.5,1.5,2)+(b4r-colour:yellow,yellow,white)[''Learning Systems/Machine Learning.''] Machine learning is a sub-field of AI which allows a machine to automatically learn from past data without specific programming instructions to do so. Often mistaken as the same thing as AI, machine learning is all about extracting knowledge from the data. Machine learning and expert systems can be similar in the aspect that they both can only perform the task designed to do. Machine learning is one of the most popular and largely developed applications of AI in society today. Machine learning programs are often used in other applications alongside regular AI programs as they allow for growth, development, and learning by the programs over time. Machine learning is frequently utilized for product suggestions by various e-commerce and entertainment companies such as Amazon and Netflix. Because of machine learning, once we look for a product on Amazon, we start seeing advertisements for the same goods while browsing the internet on the same browser. <img src="https://static.javatpoint.com/tutorial/machine-learning/images/applications-of-machine-learning.png"/> Image Found on: https://www.javatpoint.com/applications-of-machine-learning <R>The development of machine learning programs can most easily be described as a life cycle because once the program accomplishes its designed purpose, it is re-trained with another set of data for another project. This is able to be done because machine learning programs have basic/default instructions that remain for the most part untouched during the different projects and unless customized for a project the data being processed by the program is the only aspect changing. The machine learning life cycle has 7 steps: Gathering Data - Data Preparation - Data Wrangling - Analyze Data - Training the Model - Testing the Model - Deployment: Machine learning programs are the main application of targeted product suggestions and this is done through the sale of our private device browsing data to private firms.<R> [[Expert Systems]] [[Neural Networks]] [[Intelligent Agents]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]] [[Natural Interface Applications]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= (b4r:"none","none","double")+(b4r-size:1.5,1.5,2)+(b4r-colour:yellow,yellow,white)[''Neural Networks''] <R>Coming soon...<R> [[Expert Systems]] [[Learning Systems]] [[Intelligent Agents]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]] [[Natural Interface Applications]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= (b4r:"none","none","double")+(b4r-size:1.5,1.5,2)+(b4r-colour:yellow,yellow,white)[''Intelligent Agents''] <R>Coming soon...<R> [[Expert Systems]] [[Learning Systems]] [[Neural Networks]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]] [[Natural Interface Applications]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= <W> (b4r:"none","none","double")+(b4r-size:1.5,1.5,2)+(b4r-colour:yellow,yellow,white)[''Natural Language Processing''] Natural Language Processing(NLP) is an AI program's (or a regular computer's) ability to understand, interpret and manipulate human languages. ''Knowledge Base:''Similar to a database, the knowledge base is responsible for the storage of all the information, rules, data, and connections that are necessary for the expert system to have total expertise on their assigned subject. In the same way that the inference engines are separated into 2 categories, the information in the knowledge bases are organized into 2 main categories, factual knowledge and heuristic knowledge. Factual knowledge is exactly as it sounds, while heuristic knowledge is based on practice, the ability to guess, evaluate, and experience. <img src="https://static.javatpoint.com/tutorial/ai/images/expert-systems-in-ai.png"/> Image Found on:https://www.javatpoint.com/expert-systems-in-artificial-intelligence <R>Coming soon...<R> [[Learning Systems|Learning Systems 01]] [[Neural Networks|Neural Networks 01]] [[Intelligent Agents|Intelligent Agents 01]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]] [[Natural Interface Applications|natural interface applications 01]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= (b4r:"none","none","double")+(b4r-size:1.5,1.5,2)+(b4r-colour:yellow,yellow,white)[''Learning Systems/Machine Learning.''] Machine learning is a sub-field of AI which allows a machine to automatically learn from past data without specific programming instructions to do so. Often mistaken as the same thing as AI, machine learning is all about extracting knowledge from the data. Machine learning and expert systems can be similar in the aspect that they both can only perform the task designed to do. Machine learning is one of the most popular and largely developed applications of AI in society today. Machine learning programs are often used in other applications alongside regular AI programs as they allow for growth, development, and learning by the programs over time. Machine learning is frequently utilized for product suggestions by various e-commerce and entertainment companies such as Amazon and Netflix. Because of machine learning, once we look for a product on Amazon, we start seeing advertisements for the same goods while browsing the internet on the same browser. <img src="https://static.javatpoint.com/tutorial/machine-learning/images/applications-of-machine-learning.png"/> Image Found on: https://www.javatpoint.com/applications-of-machine-learning <R>Coming soon...<R> [[Expert Systems|Expert Systems 01]] [[Neural Networks|Neural Networks 01]] [[Intelligent Agents|Intelligent Agents 01]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]] [[Natural Interface Applications|natural interface applications 01]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= <R>Coming soon...<R> [[Expert Systems|Expert Systems 01]] [[Learning Systems|Learning Systems 01]] [[Intelligent Agents|Intelligent Agents 01]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]] [[Natural Interface Applications|natural interface applications 01]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= <R>Coming soon<R> [[Expert Systems|Expert Systems 01]] [[Learning Systems|Learning Systems 01]] [[Neural Networks|Neural Networks 01]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]] [[Natural Interface Applications|natural interface applications 01]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= <R>Open-source image generators like Stable diffusion use text prompts entered by the user to search the internet for images that match the prompts. Once enough data has been found, the program scraps, modifies and combines parts of multiple images to avoid direct copyright infringement. The process of morphing text prompts into custom images is called Diffusion and is extremely complex. From my perspective, this process seems a lot like a form of high-tech plagiarism.<R> <W> ''Image generated by Stable Diffusion when given the prompt: "A normal family having a picnic on a blanket in <R>Stability.AI, the company that developed Stable Diffusion, trained the program using the LAION-5B data set of images created by the German non-profit firm LAION. LAION collected these images from the internet by filtering out images with watermarks and non-relevant images like logos. <R> Andy Baio, a technologist and writer downloaded and analyzed 12 of the 600 million images used in the LAION-5B data set. In doing this, he discovered that a large portion of the images came from 3rd party websites like Pinterest as well as ArtStation, where independent artists display and sell their art to the public. [[Try Stable Diffusion out]] [[Why are they unethical/Why do digital artists care?]](align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= <R>I am not the only person dealing with this issue, other artists have begun to call out programs like Stable Diffusion for their unsanctioned use of their art. <R> One of the leaders of this movement, Karla Ortiz, and her supporters, claim that the creation of art is so closely linked with an individual, that allowing image-generating AI programs to develop unchecked will exasperate current issues and bring rise to new data protection and privacy issues. This group is still establishing its foundations, however, its first objective is to push for the introduction of new or reformed policies and regulations to better control the data usage of image-generating AI. One of the group's proposed policy changes is to restrict the training of these AI programs to data within the public domain. If the companies developing the AI want to use data from outside the public domain, they would have to seek out and forge private agreements and partnerships with each of the artists (or whoever holds the distribution rights). [[Temporary Solution | Have I been trained?]] [[Permanent Solution | Pay-Per-Play]] [[Content Authenticity Intiative]] [[Why do they use so much of Rutkowski's art?]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= <R>Stability.AI clearly states on the Stable Diffusion website, that the license agreement does not permit people to use the generated images in a way that breaks any laws or regulations. Instead of developing or choosing a new training data set that won't allow the program to generate unlawful images, Stability.AI places the responsibility of using the generated images in ethical and legal ways on the user.<R> The rising popularity of text-image AI generation programs is a concerning trend for digital artists like myself for many reasons. Firstly and perhaps the most concerning, if these programs continue to run the way they do, they will eventually eliminate the demand for our products and essentially our jobs. Our would-be customers can now get custom art pieces that would have taken an artist hours to create, instantly generated for free. Secondly, the increased popularity of text-image AI generators has oversaturated the market with art pieces that have artists' names attached to them but are not theirs. This means that when a potential customer enters an artist’s name into google, they will be presented with so many art pieces with the artist's name attached that it would be hard for them to differentiate between what is made by the artist and what is generated by an AI. In most cases, AI image generators do not provide the artists with a choice in whether or not their artwork is used by the program. Multiple artists claim to have contacted Stability.AI about removing their work from their database but have not received anything as much as an acknowledgement. Many artists argue that art is an expression of an individual's personal feelings and unique creativity which makes it so closely related to an individual that its creation should be restricted to humans only. It’s not only digital artists dealing with this issue, conventional artists, photographers, models, actors/actresses, directors, and cinematographers (pretty much anyone who digitally publishes images/videos on the internet), all run the risk of having their copyright-protected work used by text-image AI generation programs. There is no arguing the fact that open-source AI is a tremendous innovation, however, similar to when computers were first introduced into society, there are problems that need to be fixed. As long as the right people are aware of these problems, they will be resolved over time as development continues and together as a community, we can strive to find the necessary balance between innovating and helping the community. [[Try Stable Diffusion out]] [[Why do they use so much of Rutkowski's art?]] [[What Can Be Done?]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= <R>Currently, copyrighted works can only be used to train image-generating AI if its usage is considered fair use, and for noncommercial purposes. Fair use is a condition within the laws of copyright that allow the limited use of protected works, with no obligation to receive permission from the licence holder beforehand. <R> Whether or not the use of a protected work can be considered fair use is dependent on each case. However, usage of work that can classify as nonprofit, educational, noncommercial, criticism, news reports, or for research purposes often qualifies as fair use. In an effort to boost domestic AI development, the UK government is considering changing laws/policies to provide AI developers with an increased amount of data available to train their programs for both commercial and noncommercial purposes. Although it might seem like this neglects the issue of artists not having a choice in the inclusion of their art in data sets, they will still hold the ability to choose where and how their work is displayed. A condition to these changes would be that AI developers are permitted to source data for training from all sources available, except specific websites. It is theorized that with these changes, the artists and AI developers will forge a ‘pay-per-play’ or subscription relationship with each other, similar to music and TV streaming services. By this, I mean that artists who don't want their art used in data sets for AI training purposes (for free), can make their art available on special websites that require a subscription from developers if they want to access the work. Although these legal changes have not yet been implemented, I believe that this approach is very promising and shows potential to be a permanent solution other countries might benefit from copying. [[Temporary Solution | Have I been trained?]] [[Content Authenticity Intiative]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]](align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[=<R>Stable Diffusion => https://huggingface.co/spaces/stabilityai/stable-diffusion-1 <R> <W>//Copy and paste the link into a new tab on Google or your browser of choice.//<W> [[Why are they unethical/Why do digital artists care?]](align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= <R>The Content Authenticity Initiative is a tech industry-wide collaborative effort to increase published content authenticity and attribution to the creator if stolen. <R> To accomplish this, the group plans to implement something similar to a creator signature, in the form of hidden code called metadata. This metadata will be attached to the content to record its historical information while published and no matter what alterations are made in any program, the content can be traced back to the original creator. Upon creation of the content, the creator will have the option to maintain their attribution or to remain anonymous. Creators or (if chosen to remain anonymous) IP holders can easily identify their content that has been stolen entirely or scraped and synthesized into something new. [[Temporary Solution | Have I been trained?]] [[Permanent Solution | Pay-Per-Play]] [[Return to Orientation Room|orientation room]](align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= AI engineers are responsible for developing, testing, and applying various artificial intelligence models. In the process of developing a new AI, AI engineers usually do the most interaction with the AI program out of the development team. Other members of the AI development team; big data engineers, data scientists, machine learning engineers, research scientists, AI data analysts, product managers, or robotics scientists, gather/manipulate/sort/develop data. The AI engineer inputs and monitors their data in the AI. Extensive and comprehensive knowledge of all, if not most, relevant programming languages is a fundamental and necessary skill for AI engineers. Alot of the most used applications of AI fall under 1 of the categories bellow, which one would you like to begin with? Red text appeares above an alcove on the wall saying ''<R>Who Is Greg Rutkowski?<R>'' Bellow in the alcove: Greg Rutkowski is a very successful digital artist from Poland who is most well known for illustrating art pieces for games like Horizon Forbidden West, Anno, Dungeons & Dragons, and Magic the Gathering. ''An Illustration made by Greg Rutkowski for a Magic the Gathering playing card called 'The Dracula Lands'.'' <img src="https://cdnb.artstation.com/p/assets/images/images/043/931/021/large/greg-rutkowski-the-dracula-lands-1200.jpg?1638647815"/> ''An Illustration made gy Greg Rutkowski for a Dungeons and Dragons - Dungeon Kit.'' <img src="https://cdnb.artstation.com/p/assets/images/images/038/932/619/large/greg-rutkowski-4.jpg?1624468939"/> //Images found on ArtStation: https://www.artstation.com/rutkowski // Rutkowski's unique style and large collection of medevil and fantasy inspired art pieces, has made his work one of the most popular prompts for AI open-source image generators like Stable Diffusion. Lexica, a website which tracks over 10 million images and prompts generateed by Stable Diffusion, Rutkowski's name has been used in prompts around 93, 000 times! Meanwhile, world famnous artisits such as Pablo Picasso, Michelangelo, and Leanardo Da Vinci only appear in prompts around 2000 times each. //From here on out, the text in red is written in the perspective of Greg Rutkowski// [[How AI Image Generators Work]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= <R>There are certain ways an artist can publish their work that would make it easier to find and more attractive to the image-generating AI programs. Most of these were done by myself, Greg Rutowski, when uploading my work and they are largely responsible for the amount my work gets used by these programs. <R> ''Factors/Features that make an image more attractive to an AI image generator:'' - A Large volume of published high-quality digital images ready for download. - Art/Images are available for sale on highly trafficked auction sites. - Bought, used, and released to the public by a third-party company. - Published with a short descriptive text (alt text) makes it more easily identifiable while the AI program searches for images that match the given prompt. [[What Can Be Done?]](align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= You put on the glasses and a green arrow appears on the ground leading you toward the door. You realize that these glasses must utilize augmented reality to place digitally created content into a real-world environment. // ~A great example of augmented reality would be the mobile game Pokemon GO.~// As you arrive at the door, "WAIT" appears over the door along with some other text beside the door. Welcome to the Greg Rutkowski perspective experience! Before you continue onto the exhibits, we would like to explain to you the museum's purpose and overarching goal. The question that this experience was made to answer is, how can the public's knowledge and experience with AI make it harder for companies to use it unethically? As artificial intelligence continues to advance and be incorporated into society, it is important for the public to educate and familiarize themselves with AI. If artificial intelligence is introduced/incorporated into an uneducated public, the companies in control of the AI could be allowed to use the AI in unethical ways. However, if the public is educated about the possible applications of AI, then they will be aware of the unethical ways that it could be used and take preventive actions. It is suggested that you keep this concept and question in mind while exploring the exhibits. Greg Rutkowski will explore a current application of unethical AI, such as the image generator known as Stable Diffusion. But before you explore these examples you must first understand who Greg Rutkowski is and why he is relevant to this topic. [[Enter Museum|Who is Greg Rutkowski]](align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= <R>2 berlin based artists, ''Holly Herndon'' and ''Mat Dryhurst'' are working together to develop tools that will allow artists and other content creators the option to choose whether or not their work is included in the training data sets. <R> Together, Holly and Mat launched a site called “Have I Been Trained”. This site provides artists with the ability to filter-search the 5.8 billion images in the data set used to train Stable Diffusion and Midjourney (another popular image generation AI), to determine if their work is present. If an artist finds something of theirs they want to bo removed, they can simply flag it and it will be removed from future data sets. I say this is only a temporary solution to the problem as there are still no policies or regulations in place to stop the companies from finding another way to source training data. It is important that you embrace these advancements, such as artificial intelligence, that are (hopefully) being developed with the intention of benefiting society. [[Yes, I will run back to the museum right now!|entrance]] [[Yes, but my bed is really comfy and there is Netflix to binge, so no|the end]] (align:"=><=")+(box:"=XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX=")[= (b4r:"none","none","double")+(b4r-size:1.5,1.5,2)+(b4r-colour:yellow,yellow,white)[''Mental Interfaces''] Mental interfaces, also known as Brain-Computer Interfaces(BCIs), take the idea of a natural user interface a step further than virtual reality. BCIs use sensors to monitor and detect alpha waves(produced by thought) from our brains, these waves are then interpreted and acted upon as instructions. In Simpler terms, a BCIs allows an individual to control a computer/program using their thoughts. The current applications of BCIs are limited as the concept is still in the development/experimental stage and requires the wearing of electroencephalograph (EEG) sensors on the skull to detect brain waves. In the not-so-distant future, these sensors will most likely be implanted on, around, or in the brain. BCI development began with cursor control on computers for people who are paralyzed and as research continued, it became clear that to those affected by neurodegenerative diseases like ALS, limb loss, paralysis, strokes, etc., this can be the most important technological advancement in decades. <img src="https://miro.medium.com/max/595/1*KZGH5hhH5NTKHexO1mUMSg.png"/> Image found on:https://www.pinterest.ca/pin/185703184608889484/?mt=login <R>While there are clear uses for this technology in assisting individuals with disabilities, military researchers are also using it to create a superior type of interface for pilots. This improved interface will allow pilots to eliminate the unavoidable delay between a decision in the brain and the action taken by their body. Before the introduction of artificial intelligence into BCI development, researchers were struggling with decoding the tremendous amount of volume collected from the alpha waves. Neuroscientists were unable to accurately decipher a person's intentions from the excess electrical activity in their brain that is being recorded in the background and translate them into the movements of a robotic arm. Fortunately, recent advancements in AI and machine learning have greatly advanced this process. AI's capability to adapt and learn from its mistakes allows it to analyze the large volume of alpha waves one by one until it identifies the correct signals that translate into an individual's movements. BCI/Mental interface programs contain similar risks to that of speech recognition programs.As there is a lack of current applications for BCI programs, I am unaware of any specific examples of unethical applications. However, the very idea of having a foreign, decision-making device implanted in my brain scares me. If BCIs operate in any way similar to regular computers, data (brain information) will have to be stored somewhere. This presents the opportunity for this data about our private memories, intentions, conscious and unconscious interests, and emotional reactions, to be sold and exploited by companies. <R> [[Natural
